RATING: 10
One of a kind. Wonderfully written. I've thought about how it could be improved, but mechanically - there is nothing. There is nothing superfluous here, no fat - ffg this isn't. The second case only took 2 but we also spent two on the third without really getting to the crux of the matter... and those were some fun hours indeed.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
SHCD combines my love of literature with my enjoyment when solving mysteries/puzzles, and was just a ton of fun for me.  I played all 10 cases solo because I enjoyed it so much after playing the first case that I couldn't wait to keep playing.

Creating this game must have been a labour of love.  I can't imagine how difficult it is to come up with even one of these cases, let alone ten + expansions.  I'm in awe of what the authors have accomplished with this game.

With that said, it does have some flaws.  Typos, unsatisfying solutions that make you want to punch Sherlock, and (perhaps inevitably) some weaker cases.  Despite its flaws, one of my favourite games of all time and I will buy all of the reprinted expansions as soon as they come out.

Note : It is best played as an activity and not a game.  Don't try to compete with Sherlock, just enjoy each case and try to visit as many locations as you can to get as much of the texture of each scenario as possible.  Don't worry about your score, just be happy if you are able to solve the case.  Some of the cases I found really challenging.

RATING: 7
A very nice choose your own adventure co-op. It is fun trying to figure out the small but important clues from the text. The storylines are interesting and twist in the plot not so obvious. However, I am afraid that after a few games you might start seeing patterns repeat themselves, i.e., it is not what you are being told but what is left unsaid that is important. This is also a game that I could truly imagine playing myself when you have all the time in the world to read over the text and you do not have vote for every decision, although haste and negotiation is part of the fun as well.

RATING: 9.5
Excellent deduction game from '81! This is not a boardgame in the common sense (cards or dice or moves or boards) but a collection of 10 cases that the player(s) must solve by gathering clues, visiting people, searching the newspapers for hints, etc. For fans of deduction games, this is so far the best game I found on the topic. What's more important, during the 2-3 hours that you will spend on the case, you will actually feel that you're visiting people, interviewing, questioning, findings hints etc.

RATING: 8.9
I am not a fan of deduction games, but this one is one glorious exception! My rating would be a 10, except for the fact that there will come an inevitable point when the limit of replayability is reached. And that is a gaming tragedy.


COMMENTS ON THE ENGLISH YSTARI EDITION: It's all quite wonderful; yet the font is, at times, challenging to decipher in both the directory and the cases. The most annoying problem, though, is the very poor proofreading job that was done (or not done?) on the text; there are many, many instances of misspellings, and (even worse) situations where isolated French words have never even been translated! This is annoying, but it still does not mar one of the best games ever made.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Consulting Detective is the more cerebral cousin of those turn to page 234 adventure books; more cerebral in that you have to figure out which page to turn to next for yourself.  The adventures in this package are pretty short and snappy, with Holmes frequently solving them in just a handful of clues.  I tend to take a longer, winding route.  This suggests to me that the level of difficulty is pitched pretty well.  

The Holmesian theming is very well done, from the scene setting introduction to each case to the copies of the Times that may contain useful information among reports from the Empire and adverts for snake oil. This was clearly a labour of love by enthusiasts for Conan Doyle's great creation.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Πολύ ενδιαφέρον παιχνίδι στο οποίο οι παίκτες σε ρόλο ντετέκτιβ προσπαθούν να λύσουν διάφορες υποθέσεις. Το κουτί περιλαμβάνει 10 σενάρια, έναν χάρτη του Λονδίνου και ένα χρυσό οδηγό με διευθύνσεις όλων των κατοίκων και των επιχειρήσεων. Επίσης περιλαμβάνονται και 10 εφημερίδες των Times μια δηλαδή για κάθε υπόθεση. :meeple:

Οπότε διαλέγουμε σενάριο, διαβάζουμε το εισαγωγικό κείμενο που αναφέρει συνήθως γενικά το τι έγινε, πότε, που και μετά είμαστε ελεύθεροι να κινηθούμε όπως θέλουμε. Μπορεί για παράδειγμα να θέλουμε να μιλήσουμε με κάποιον αυτόπτη μαρτυρα, βρίσκουμε την διευθυνσή του στο χρυσό οδηγό και μετά διαβάζουμε το αντίστοιχο κείμενο στο βιβλίο της υπόθεσης. Πολλές φορές βρίσκουμε στοιχεία και στην εφημερίδα της τότε ημέρας. ;)

Συνεχίζουμε με αυτό τον τρόπο μέχρι να πιστέψουμε ότι λύσαμε το μυστήριο και μετά απαντάμε σε κάποιες ερωτήσεις και βγάζουμε μια βαθμολογία ανάλογα με το αν απαντήσαμε σωστά αλλά και πόσες επισκέψεις χρησιμοποιήσαμε σε σχέση με τον Χολμς που λύνει και αυτός την υπόθεση παράλληλα με εμάς. Φυσικά υπάρχει και η αιτιολόγηση από τον Χολμς για το πως έλυσε την υπόθεση σε χρόνο dt. :cool:
 
Ουσιαστικά δεν πρόκειτε για επιτραπέζιο αφού δεν έχει καθόλου πιόνια, ταμπλό, κάρτες ή ζάρια, παρά μόνο κείμενο. Μαζευόμαστε με την παρέα, βάζουμε ανάλογη μουσική (προτείνω ambient μουσική από βικτωριανή αγγλία, άμαξες να περνάνε) αράζουμε στο καναπέ με κάνα μπουκάλι κρασί, κρατάμε σημειώσεις και αρχίζουμε τις θεωρίες. Περισσότερο σε γκρουπ activity φέρνει. Δεν μπορέσαμε ποτέ να κερδίσουμε τον Χολμς αλλά έχουμε και άλλα 5 σενάρια να δοκιμάσουμε. Who knows?  :p
  
Το παιχνίδι προσφέρει λοιπόν μια διαφορετικού τύπου εμπειρία πράγμα πολύτιμο σε ένα χόμπυ που λόγω υπερβολικής και συνεχής παραγωγής νέων παιχνιδιών καταλήγεις να βρίσκεις σχεδόν όλα τα παιχνίδια όμοια μεταξύ τους αφού δεν υπάρχει ο χρόνος και ο χώρος για να ξεχωρίσει κάποιο παιχνίδι.  

Συστήνεται ανεπιφύλακτα σε λάτρεις αστυνομικών υποθέσεων. Σε βάζει για τα καλά στο κλίμα της εποχής ενώ και ο τρόπος γραφής είναι πολύ κοντά στο πρωτότυπο. Προσοχή μόνο στην υπόθεση 3 που έχει λάθη. Εκτυπώστε τις διορθώσεις προτού την δοκιμάσετε. Δοκιμάστε επίσης και μερικά fan made σενάρια γατί το expansion αργεί ακόμα. :p

RATING: 8
I have only tried the first case solo so far.

It was a really cool experience. It really immerses you in the Conan Doyle's books atmosphere, and it is for sure a challenging deduction exercise.

However, I just felt close to impossible to figure out the solution following a number of clues that is close to the Sherlock benchmark. Maybe it will become easier if I play it cooperatively with a couple of friends.

Or maybe just forget about the benchmark and play the game competitively.

But it sure needs a playing group that is willing to engage with the format of this unique experience. And willing to read a lot too.

Tras 5 casos se agotó la paciencia y... patada a seguir.

RATING: 10
I absolutely love this game.

It's simply, easy to learn, and consists of pure deduction and mystery-solving fun! You play one of the "Baker Street Irregulars", aka you solve the cases Sherlock doesn't have time for.

The replay-ability is limited because once you know the answers to the cases, it's hard/near-impossible to replay them. Also the translation from French to English left behind a few errors, that are more annoying that actually detrimental to gameplay. Normally, these cons might lower my rating, but the good things about the games outshine these minor problems. So other than that, this game is solid and a MUST for any game collection.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Régen voltam ilyen gondban játékértékeléskor. Nagyon különleges játékról beszélünk.

Kezdjük azzal, hogy teljesen egyedülálló szerintem, hogy egy olyan játékot, ami a 80-as években (gondolom) sikeres volt, aztán 20 évig nem adták ki, feledésbe merült, majd 2010 után előkaparták, és újra népszerű legyen. Itt ez történt. Az Ystari előszedte, leporolta és kiadta, majd pár éven belül a top100-ba ért. A merész az volt a dologban, hogy szerintem 2010-ig a BGG userek 1%-a ha hallott róla, tehát nem egy bejáratott névről volt szó. Szerencsére az Ystarinál valaki bízott benne, felkereste a szerzőket, stb.

A másik, ami miatt egyedülálló a játék, az a fizikai tartalma. Gyakorlatilag a térképen kívül csak füzetecskéket kapunk: egy névjegyzéket, egy szabálykönyvet, 10 újságot (=2 oldalas A3-asok), és 10 sztorifüzetet. Összesen 2-300 oldalnyi tömény szöveget, semmi mást. Nincs dobókocka. Nincs token. Nincs kis kocka, nincs figura, nincs semmi. Nyilván fakkos dobozbelső sem:) Egy doboz és benne egy könyvre való szöveg.

Ebből következőn messze a legnyelvfüggőbb játék, amit valaha próbáltam. Megjegyzem, direkt azzal a céllal vettem, hogy jó lesz nyelvgyakorlásra, úgyis azt mondják, kezdésként jók a detektívkönyvek, mert viszonylag rövidek, és hamar kiderül hogy értjük-e. Itt elérkeztünk az egyik problémához: némi szótárazgatással ment ugyan a dolog, de a folyamatos fordítás rányomta a bélyeget a játékélményemre. Vagyis az angolja nekem nehéz kicsit (ráadásul a nyomtatásnál használt betűtípus sem a legjobb). Hogy viszonyítani lehessen: Nehezebb, mint a játékszabályok, azokhoz már nem nagyon használok szótárat. Ehhez kellett. És nagyon nagy mennyiség. Az ügy felvázolása kb. 2 oldal volt, és némelyik helyszín szintén volt vagy 1 oldal, és mi jártunk vagy 15 helyszínen. És akkor még ott volt az újság is. És mivel itt minden szónak jelentősége van, alaposnak kellett lenni. És azért játék közben szótárazgatni órákon át nem túl vicces. Tanulság: legközelebb úgy ülök le, hogy legyen egy profi angolos a csapatban. Egyébként azt olvastam, hogy könnyű a nyomozós része, de nekünk szerintem részben a nyelvi kínlódás miatt nem volt könnyű, erre elment minden figyelmem, nem nagyon tudtam magára az ügyre koncentrálni. Ezzel együtt nem jártunk annyira messze... (gondolom ebből kiderült, hogy a csapatban, ami 2 főt jelentett, én tudtam legjobban angolul)

Másik amit problémának lehet nevezni az értékelésnél, hogy ez szerintem nem is annyira a klasszikus értelemben vett társasjáték, inkább színtiszta rejtvény, vagy rejtély megfejtés. Ez nem baj, mert szeretek ilyeneken agyalni, de szerintem teljesen más a célcsoportja mint mondjuk a legtöbb közismert társasnak. Ha ezt lefordítanák és kitennék a tescoba, simán vinnék olyanok is, akik életükben nem társasoztak, és ettől nem is feltétlen jönne meg a kedvük úgy általában a társasokhoz, de lehet hogy tökre bejönne nekik mint rejtélymegoldó játék. Tehát ez egy teljesen külön kategória, lehet hogy ezzel is magyarázható a sikere. Még csak hasonlót se láttam a piacon.

Összességében nagyon tematikus és letisztult. Aki szereti úgy általában a krimit, a nyomozgatós filmeket-könyveket, az szeretni fogja. A kelléktár egyszerű. Van egy sztori, és a névjegyzéket meg a térképet meg az újságokat használhatjuk, és a helyszínekről kapunk infót az ügyhöz tartozó kis füzetből. Jegyzetelhetünk és a végén kérdésekre kell válaszolni. Még megoldókulcs is van, Sherlock levezeti, hogy kellett volna megoldani. Szerintem nagyon elegáns, hogy mondjuk az 5. ügynél az összes korábbi újság is használható, bár még ott nem járok, de feltételezem hogy van is értelme, ha kitér rá a szabály, tehát akadnak a régebbi újságokban is információmorzsák a későbbiekre vonatkozóan.

Felmerülhet az újrajátszhatóság. Jogosan. Összesen 10 ügy van. De egyrészt vannak kiegek (igaz eddig főleg csak franciául), másrészt 1-1 ügy megoldása nem két perc. És valahogy ez nem az a játék, amit mondjuk hetente elő akarnék venni, tehát engem nem zavar hogy csak 10 ügy van. Évente tartunk néhány nyomozást, és mire a végére érünk már lehet hogy nem emlékszünk a régebbi ügyek csattanójára. Megjegyzem, a névjegyzék pl. már némelyik kieghez szükséges adatokat is tartalmazza.

A játék nagy pozizívuma, hogy szinte tetszőleges létszámmal játszható, és lehet egymás ellen és coop módban is.

Nyomozni szeretőknek mindenképp ajánlom, de ismerjék jól az idegen nyelvet:)

Eszembe jutott a játék egy nagy hibája: reprodukálható sima fénymásolással...

---
Az első 3 sztorin vagyunk túl. A durva nyelvfüggőség miatt eladtam, de nem zárom ki, hogy még játszom majd valaha vele. Negatívum, hogy volt olyan sztori, amit nem éreztünk elég egzaktnak (a 3.-at). Elég érdekes egyébként, hogy mekkora szórás van a sztorik terjedelmében. A helyszínek szövegei van ahol csak 6 oldalt tesznek ki, máshol 20+ oldalt. Amit fontosnak tartok, hogy kis kockákat tehettek volna a játékba, mi házilag szedtünk elő párat, mert jó a bejárt és/vagy szóbajövő helyszíneket más-más színnel jelölgetni.

3 parti alapján a játék legnagyobb erősségének a hangulatát tartom.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
You'd think that getting to crack just 10 murder mystery scenarios without any replay value is the sort of Baker Street dozen that will make you feel short changed, but then you'd have missed the vital clue: it is a Baker St one. This is one of the most atmospheric games I have ever played, and the makers have gone to extraordinary lengths to evoke the spirit of the Times.

You will never get closer to donning the mantle of Sherlock, and if you indeed manage to close cases with the bare minimum of clues you are certainly worthy of it. Boy these babies are well written. They are perfect solo material, but it's a waste to do them on your own. It's the sort of game that makes you want to boast about your cleverness afterwards. Well, celebrating that one moment of genius anyway, rather than being reminded of the long clue-hunt around town, figuring out that what was bleeding obvious to someone who had studied the play aids with a bit more imaginative attention. Yes, some cases can be cracked with just 2 clues, but only if you have the Sherlock genes. It won't stop most of us getting lost in the London fog for quite a bit longer than that, but the thrill of unravelling the intertwined plot-lines that wee bit slower doesn't make it less enjoyable for the slow puzzlers amongst us. There are several roads to solve a case, with a generous sprinkling of red herrings to keep you on your toes, spread across 50-odd locations per case. Sometimes the slow solvers are the only ones to encounter all aspects of a case, and can actually beat the score of the "perfect sleuths" by knowing more of the background story. It's a wonderful mechanic.

This one oozes atmosphere. It is the little period details that are slipped in, about late 19th century events and developments that do a wonderful job at keeping up the illusion. I know few games that drag you into the setting as effortlessly as this gem, it is all you could want it to be. It is an experience so entirely immersing that at the end you do wish you had your own little pocket Watson to write up the newspaper column detailing your private roadmap to the grand unveiling.

This isn't Cluedo or any of the other usual suspects, where it has to be one of a limited amount of abstract permutations. No Mrs White, in the Library, with the Rope. The cases are well written, as colourful as any of the Conan Doyle plots, and it will take some mental agility to find the quickest way to crack a case. The initial scene is presented with a small introduction of a few paragraphs, but it's up to you to spot the clues, study the map of London, race around town using the phonebook to pin down the less obvious locations, and put the newspaper clippings to good use. And use your petite grey cells, mon ami. It reminds me of my childhood days with Jumbo's Orient Express, which also had genuine cases to solve, but they are no match for the quality, complexity, and impressive Victorian period detail on offer here (with only the occasional annoying Americanism, in writing that ought to be solid Queen's English). What they do have in common is the pressure to make "that tricky call". You know that you can hang around for a couple more turns to obtain clues that will confirm (or waylay) your suspicions, but you know it's a race against time, and the real challenge is to call it as early as possible. When you play it competitively it is great to hear others present their solutions to the case. That's usually the point when doubt about your own version of events starts to creep in, no matter how sure you were when you jotted it down.

Fact: it is put together with great eye for detail, fairly unique in its approach, feels more like interactive fiction than a conventional game, and equally enjoyable as a solo, competitive, or co-operative game. Fact: it is a labour of love, the setting research and ambiance is on a par with the best Call of Cthulhu RPG scenarios, compiled with the same fanatical attention for detail. Fact: ten cases isn't nearly enough, but thankfully there are expansions. If there was an endless amount of cases to solve, it's elementary, it would score a solid 10 my dear Watson.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Fantastic, you can play alone or in cooperative play.

RATING: 9
Less a typical board game and more of an elaborate pick-a-path book that puts you in the shoes of Holmes's proteges and tasks you with solving a unique Baker St mystery. Each of the ten cases included in the box is a one-off puzzle to be solved, and they are really well written and tough to work out. There is no hand-holding, and players will have to use all their powers of logic and investigation to figure out whodunnit. Technically you're competing as a team against Holmes, but that bastard always figures it out in about four turns, so really it's just a joy to work together to nut out the whos, hows and whys and then find out [i]you were right[/i]. Perfect game for couples.

RATING: 7
I'm quite torn on this game. On the one hand I absolutely loved the way it made me feel while we were playing. It was like reading an actual murder mystery novel and trying to come up with the solution before the detective does it for you. It led to lots of interesting discussions amongst the group, and we came up with a ton of intriguing theories. Yet after all this fun deduction and debate, we read the solution and I felt there was not a chance for us to come up with those answers. I even reexamined clues that we never read, and saw no conceivable way they could have led us to that solution. I'm fine with them sowing lots of red herrings into the game and making it tough on the detectives, but it should at least be possible when the right path is taken. I also fear the replayability is just a bit too low to be worth the cost. I understand that this is inevitable because of the amount of detail they put into each mystery, but since the solutions are so memorable, I don't think you could ever replay the same mystery. In the end I think it's a good game, because I can't deny the pure enjoyment I experienced while playing, I just wish it was executed slightly different.

RATING: 8
Consulting Detective is so thematical that playing it really feels like a Sherlock Holmes story, if only slightly apocryphal: as such, it stands in the twilight zone between proper boardgames and diceless RPGs but doesn’t belong to either, as on the one side its rules are both too loose for a boardgame and dangerously close to an RPG’s whilst on the other they don’t provide players with as much free hand as any RPG would.

Anyhow, playing Consulting Detective is a great fun: sadly, it lacks in anything random, which makes replaying a scenario impossible as soon as you know what the plot was, where the relevant testimonies are and, even more so, how Sherlock Holmes’ preternatural deduction skills got the case solved.

This makes for its major - and likely only - downside as well.

RATING: 9
I have the Sleuth Publications original Consulting Detective and the first expansion, The Mansion Murders. I remember distinctly playing with one of the authors at a game convention in Chicago in 1982 or '83. On the strength of that one tough play, I bought the game and the first expansion—but could never convince anyone at home to play. Slaying goblins in D&D or sinking third-rates in WS&IM was the order of the day with my group most of the time.

I've been eyeing the Ystari/Asmodee reprint for some time and have finally secured a copy in English. I look forward to giving this unique game a second chance with a new cotorie of players. I'm sure, with games like Tales of the Arabian Nights and Star Trek: the Adventure Game already having traction, I can find someone else to give it a spin. I would play solo, but that just doesn't seem like much fun to me. But I will certainly do that with the new game, if necessary.

The production in this new edition is top-notch, though the syntax for the English edition could have stood another pass with a native speaker. The one clear advantage of the original game over the new: the original made lavish use of the old Sydney Paget Strand magazine illustrations and I quite miss them in the new game, though a new generation of gamers is really not missing anything. Just a touch that gave the original some welcome period feeling. I'll be happy to report on this one again when I have some cases under my belt.

Update 12.07.2012: Played my first full game with three other players in cooperative. We managed to solve the case of the munitions magnate in 23 leads and answering all questions at the end correctly. Holmes finished the case in 4 leads and the case granted us 4 "gimmes" for places visited. Our final score was 65.

Our table was pleased, for its first try. We might have had a score of 75, but we visited Holmes and the Yard, which were unneccessary based on the amount of evidence already gathered.

It was a great time!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've only played this solo so I can't speak to the multiplayer experience. The idea of the game and the feel of the game as it's played are like nothing else. It really feels like you're on a mission; I put a lot of pressure on myself to try to unpack the solution against the measure of the game. Asa fan I will offer one warning: one problem is that sometimes the solution and the solitaire measure of success - Holmes' course through the mystery - aren't entirely fair as they are presented. Red herrings abound and often times leaps of association are expected, most often in Holmes' solutions, and of a type that would go unrewarded nine times out of ten. One scores points in this game by solving the mystery in the fewest possible steps - which means that while you're playing it, a major goal is actually to experience LESS of what the game has provided you. Tightening up of some of the cases and the text of the clues would solve this, I think. Still, if it sounds like I'm being too critical, understand that this criticism comes from the occasional frustration with a game I love to play. That criticism only is really relevant for solitaire play, too, as more than one player would be dealing with the same obstacles. I am sorely hoping for English language expansions; I would purchase them immediately.

RATING: 9
I would love to give this game a 10.  It's truly unique, exciting in a group or simply enthralling in solo play.  Average play time per mission for me has been about 4 or 5 hours of intense contemplation of evidence and facts, reading news papers, and trying to read my gut feelings.  After all of this I truly feel like a detective, and if this sounds like fun to you, you're probably right.  
  This being said, there are some problems with the game.  There are numerous typos.  Much of the language in the books is antiquated, meaning you're probably going to consult google at least a couple times to find the meaning of a word.  Sometimes you're going to then realize that the word you're looking up doesn't exist and then try to figure out what they meant to right there.  As particularly potent example, in one of the cases the editor did a find and replace to change all instanced of "die" to "the"  And it took a while to figure out why so many people had "thed" until we found out about a certain professors "stuthes."  There are some solutions which are accurate for older versions of the game, but were not updated to reflect changes to the story in the newer edition.  They're pretty easy to spot and figure out exactly what was changed though.  Also be warned, most of the cases are great, but case 3 is complete rubbish.
  If you are willing to accept these flaws, you're in for some of the hardest game play out there, but with enough work, instinct, and attention to detail they are all solvable, although sometimes - just barely.  You'll probably fail a few, and slap your forehead saying "Oh, it was right there the whole time!  But it was so easy to assume it wasn't"  When you do get the solution right though it feels amazing, because you know exactly how the game was stacking the odds against you.
  Good luck sleuths!

RATING: 7.75
This is a very unique game that is a bit of a gem amongst the modern scene.  It's a paragraph driven game whose sole mechanic relies on you following clues to various locations (a suspect's address, the scene of the crime, the coroner's office for more information, etc.).  You have a number of tools at your disposal to further refine your lead selection and formulate your hypothesis on who the murderer was and what of his/her motivation.

It's so different from anything else you will play that I urge anyone with even an inkling of interest in deduction games to check it out.  It's pure, engaging, and addictive.

My full review can be found at: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/1015917/my-favorite-game-featuring-1888-british-newspaper

RATING: 10
UPDATE, 1/7: Consulting Detective is a hard game. It is hard enough just solve the case, let alone beat it faster, or with more points, than Sherlock. The key is to remember that you aren't simply deducing the solution from known facts that you uncover as you move around London, but that you are actually trying to imaginatively find a hypothesis that fits those facts. Many cases require intuition and vision, or maybe even psychic powers, to solve completely. In other words, you have to find the solution the same way Holmes does: through creative work, careful (and by that I mean CAREFUL) attention to detail, and rigorous sleuthing. Making the assumption that you can solve the mysteries by going from lead to lead until the truth reveals itself in facts that follow coherently from one to another will probably lead to frustration. Finding the connections between clues and reconstructing the crime scene require a writerly imagination as much as a logical mind.

New plan of attack: Five cases in, I think I'm going to quit worrying about even trying to beat Sherlock and just spend as much time as possible in this Victorian London world tracking down leads and enjoying the writing and world-building of this brilliantly-imagined game. My impatience to solve the cases as fast as possible has lead to my missing important clues.

UPDATE, 12/30: The new Asmodee is great, if a little too glossy for my tastes. My original rating (see below) was based on solitaire play. Having played it cooperatively now, I absolutely adore this game. Consulting Detective is a thematic and fun as any other game I own. Like my other recent favorites ASL and High Frontier, SHCD is immersive in exactly the way I love: you actually 'feel' your way into the Holmes' Victorian world. 

Unlike TotAn or CYOA, which I find limiting in ways that aren't as quite as satisfying, in SH you feel more free to move about its world because the nature of mystery storytelling encourages you to limit your choices (by racing against Holmes) and stay "on script" (by only following up on viable leads). The lovely writing, despite the occasional typos and mistranslations, paints in the edges of the canvas in a way that encourages a deeper narrative-immersion than ToTAN (which I still love). What a disappointment to see a game as engrossing and original as Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective sit in the 300's on BGG with all the cookie-cutter dreck between it and the top 10.

I have very little interest in playing Consluting Detective competitively; the game is hard enough with a team of detectives and a good part of the fun is reading outloud with the other players and discussing the next best step. As with all co-ops, beware the bossy-pants alpha-male gamer!

Caution: Consulting Detective is not like any other game I've played. It combines (light) literature and gaming into a hybrid art that works wonderfully as gaming-lit. It requires literacy, patience, and the ability to allow oneself to be teleported to and immersed in another world through the cooperative use of imagination. The mysteries are difficult and occasionally frustrating, requiring leaps in logic that involve imaginative reconstruction rather than simple deduction from known facts. This can give the impression that the cases are either flawed or just too damn hard, but close attention to the solutions and Holmes's thinking usually reveals each case's inner coherence. 

Potential downsides: 1. The solutions can sometimes be really obscure. 2. It might be impossible to beat the case in fewer leads than Sherlock, though I think outscoring him is possible thanks to the tangential mysteries that each case contains. 3. The strange and old-fashioned nature of the gameplay (reading outloud, etc.) may turn off gamers who have limited imagination, who lack of patience, or who are uninterested in the theme. The lack of replayibility, while sad, makes each case sweeter in the same way that meditating on the fact that you're only allotted so many sunrises ought to make each day a little sweeter. Limits make things beautiful and help you appreciate them. Plus, unlike life, there is the potential for expansions. 

ORIGINAL COMMENTS: I guess I'm not a big fan of Sherlock Holmes.  I found this slightly boring.  There are better paragraph based boardgames out there.  Strictly for Holmes fans in my opinion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Neat! Really feels like solving a mystery. Interactive fiction. The flavor is great.

Personally, I'm not a fan of being penalized for following leads. To me, the fun is in experiencing the whole "story" rather than just being as efficient as possible. I'm happy to play and ignore points and just see if I can solve the mystery, frankly.

We played the recent Ystari edition and the script the booklets are written in is irritating. It can be hard to read. In this case, I would have preferred function over flavor.

The game also feels a little long for just being a puzzle. Some of the flavor text sections are a bit too long. If these were trimmed, it'd probably move a bit faster. But even so completing this in an hour seems unlikely.

All in all though, cool unique game. I'd say if you grew up liking Choose Your Own Adventure books you'd probably like this too!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.2
Amazing game, simple mechanics but it delivers a great experience if you’re into deduction games. It really tests your logical and deduction skills as well as your imagination when you hit a dead-end.

Played the first three cases so far with my gf and we have noticed that it’s better to play it when you have enough time ahead of you so you don’t rush deductions. Follow leads, take detailed notes, build timelines, study the map carefully, and take your time analyzing your data. Taking breaks or playing over multiple sessions (not too spread though) also helps, as it gives you a chance to clear your head and come back with new ideas.

Trying to beat Sherlock is not really worth it. It will most likely lead to missing large part of the story or wrong deductions. We’ve found that it’s better if you first try to get the full picture of what happened, and then worry about how many leads you’ve used. If you care about final score and how you fare against Sherlock, then think very carefully when deciding which lead to follow.

I think the best player count is 2 as it  allows you to exchange ideas while the game remains easy to follow. With many people and some of them having less patience than others might spoil the fun.

Case #1: 95 points
Case #2: 30 points (missed important leads and rushed it)
Case #3: 80 points
Case #5: 105 points

Played the corrected version (2016-2).

RATING: 10
In this game, you are a member of the Baker Street Irregulars that try to solve the mystery along with or before Sherlock. It was created in the 80's and was translated from French to English (for some reason they don't go back and fix mistranslations)

Out of the gate i'm going to go ahead and say that you and your husband will love this game. I would highly recommend it for a couple's game only. You can play with really as many people as you want but I LOVE the time and adventure that my wife and I have during the game.

It is not a typical board game as you only have a Case booklet, Map of Sherlock's London, a London Directory (corresponds with locations on the map) and newspapers.

To start a game you read the beginning of the Case booklet where you learn the details of the case in 221B Baker Street with Sherlock and Holmes. At the end of the beginning details, you are off (without Sherlock or Holmes) to decide where in London you need to go and learn more about the case.

As you visit places on the map, let's say you want to visit the brother of the deceased. You look up the brother in the directory, 54NW, and look that location up in the Case booklet and read the paragraph(s) with it to learn more information.

My wife and I and I played it our first game and we took meticulous notes and played over the course of 12 hours. I KNOW THAT'S A LONG TIME but it was so much fun. You can realistically play it as long or as short as you want OR you can play it over the stretch of several days.

We just so happen to have been able to have the kiddos at the grandparents the days that we played the 1st and 2nd case. We went a LOT faster on the 2nd case as we kind of knew what we needed to do. We even took it with us to dinner and talked about the case there and read stuff in the car.

I will warn you that it is only 10 cases and there is little to no replay-ability. BUT would you rather love and to never love again that to have never watched the show Firefly? TOTALLY worth it.

RATING: 9
I've only played this once, but what a fantastic experience it was. You really do feel like a detective slowly piecing together a case. The thing that caught me off guard (and the thing I love about this the most, honestly) is that there wasn't a clue or sequence of events you'll find that spells out what happened. Nobody said "Okay, you got me, I did this." It's all shrouded in ambiguity and you have to make judgement calls - just like in real life.

Oh, and Sherlock's solution at the end will make you feel like an absolute idiot.

I can't wait to play this again.

Edit: I PLAYED THIS AGAIN. I really did not like the second case nearly as much as the first. Without spoilers, I feel that it was not constructed as well. I'm still very excited to try the rest of the cases.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
When you take three types of games that I already love and mix them together, you just know I'm going to give it a good rating.  SHCD mixes deduction skills with a cooperative format, while leading you on a "Choose Your Own Adventure" goose chase.  Can you solve the mystery?  And how quickly?

Players are given a thorough background on the case at hand, and then as a group decide what leads to follow - and those choices are many.  Each lead corresponds to a numbered entry to read (think Tales of the Arabian Nights) and you keep track of how many leads are used.  When the group feels ready, you tackle some questions about the case, each giving a set number of points for a correct answer.  Deduct points for taking too many leads and see how you did!  If you beat 100, you outfoxed Holmes himself!

Delightful and atmospheric, this game's only real drawback is a limited number of these complex cases.  It's just begging to have more researched or translated.  Speaking of which - the English translation can be very rough - you've been warned.

RATING: 9
Really fun, and very alternative experience compared to most 'board games'.
The stories are really fun, and very exciting. However, some of the answers or solutions require some silly, illogical jumps of logic, whereas others make you think 'aha' in the most awesome way.

Pros:
Cool mysteries, with very exciting solution paths
Get some chills sometimes when the clues all start to pan out
Nicely made newspapers, cases and directory

Cons:
Some silly solutions
Quite a few typos
Silly stuff like needing to find a street name on the map, which is bloody difficult
Limited play (understandably)

Awesome game, would always play it if others are up for it!

Elementary/10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Offers 10 very challenging mysteries, of which I completed only 5. During all these cases my group would frequently get stuck and wonder if we had everything figured out, or if we'd missed something (usually it was the latter). I found most of the cases I played to be difficult and frustrating, and we often got nowhere near the answer. I found it hard to judge when we knew enough about a case to go to the questions; the decision to finally face the questions was normally accompanied by a feeling of exhaustion or resignation, even if we were (usually mistakenly) pretty confident we had a good handle on the case.

There is a pressure to use as few leads as possible, but the questions could be about all sorts of tangential aspects of a case that one might not have encountered despite establishing the big picture. Perhaps having some questions in advance to guide the investigation might make the experience less frustrating, but as it is, looking at the given questions ahead of time would spoil the case.

I can see what the positive reviewers see in the game. There are those who report that they figured out every case and had a great time doing it, so I won't claim that it's broken or too difficult. It just hasn't worked for the the eight or nine people who've played it with me.

RATING: 8
This is more of an atmospheric puzzle than a game. It's also a game I remember playing as a teenager and has been out of print until recently. There are no real rules to speak of other than the mechanics of visiting a place/person and looking up the corresponding section in the case file, and it's entirely up to you how long you want to play for - you might finish a case in an hour or play over a couple of nights.

When we play it we're absorbed in the whodunnit, taking notes, drawning connections between suspects on post-its on the wall, reading and re-reading the newspapers for clues (yes, the game has newspapers), trying to decide who did what. If you're a reader, and especially if you like the detective/crime genre, it's well worth a look.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Sherlock Holmes Consulting detective is an extremely story centered game which will put you against the master of deduction itself. 10 cases to resolve full of intrigue and Victorian age environment immersion. It will make you feel like being right in the spot, living the London aura testing your mind and deduction power.
I personally had high hopes for the game; unfortunately.. they were shattered soon after i started to play the game.
Being exclusively based on story, its language level reflect the age it represents (if you can't understand any single word of this review, by any means don't get the game). The connections between the clues are somehow circumstantial and made me feel not satisfied even with Holmes resolution (i felt there never was a final definitive proof).
In addition this game supports 8 players and, even if it could handle more as there's no real meaning to limit it to 8, it has to be clear that the game is the ONLY reason why you're all sitting at the table and the only interaction you're going to have with the other players is because you're discussing the clues. Any other break, interruption, phone call, etc will only interrupt either the story flow (making you read multiple times the same line) or your line of thoughts forgetting clues or possible leads.
In conclusion this definitely not a bad game and the price is not prohibitive either but you have to know in advance what you're throwing yourself into.

Sehr interessantes und weitgehend unbekanntes Spiel des Jahres 1985 das seiner Zeit weit voraus war. Das ist eigentlich gar kein Brettspiel, sondern ein Krimi-Rätsel-Spiel. Es gibt kaum Brettspiel-artige Mechanismen, man muss den Fall wirklich durch Überlegen, einem Stadtplan und einem Adressbuch lösen, indem man verschiedene Orte besucht und nachliest was für Informationen man dort findet. Das Spiel nimmt die Spieler nicht an die Hand, sondern man muss wirklich selbst draufkommen was passiert ist. Das ist sehr ungewöhnlich, aber auch ziemlich herausfordernd, sprich schwer. Wenn man die richtigen Leute am Tisch hat, kann das Knobeln an einem Fall sehr spaßig sein.

RATING: 5
Players are the Sherlock Holmes street gang, helping the great detective solve ten mysterious cases.  Cooperative story game, where a crime is described, and you go out and "interact" with London by visiting various people and reading out their statements.  Gradually, the plot will be revealed, the clues collated, and several questions asked at the end of the game.  Points are tallied against correct answers to determine a winner.  You are also graded against the great man, who solves the cases with astonishing ease.  Fun game, but not for everyone.  The Ystari reprint is very nice, but with some "interesting" type/font choices.

RATING: 7.5
Two cases down, and it's been a lot of fun. My wife really enjoys this game. It gives her the thrill of poking around in people's business. For me, I know it's a good game because of the amount of time I spend thinking about each case (and discussing with my wife) after the game is over.

The only negatives for me are: (1) the font. There is a lot of reading in this game, and the font sacrifices clarity for style, and (2) because every word is scrutinized in this game, even a few small editing errors can really cause a lot of frustration.

Played Case 4. Reading back through previous case newspapers is a bit of a drag.

RATING: 7
Really one of the best co-operative games I can ever think of playing. Perfect for couples. The cases are interesting and you genuinely feel like Sherlock Holmes as you have little eureka moments together which push you forward. 
    I'm not a fan of having to include all the previously used newspapers for each new case - it just feels like work. Cases are so difficult that reading all the papers thoroughly is a must unless you miss something essential to you being successful. 
    Deciding when to end the game is odd too, you never feel like you've gathered enough intel to be able to answer whatever sherlock is going to ask you in his final confrontation. Go too soon and the questions make you feel like you haven't gotten your moneys worth out of the case (that you will never play again). Go too late and its highly unlikely that your going to beat Sherlock. 
It is still rewarding if you can answer just a few of Sherlock's questions though. 
    Ticks a unique box in my collection and I always enjoy playing.

RATING: 9.35
This was a surprise, this game is AMAZING. There's no board, no cards and no tokens, just a map of London, the 1888 London Directory and a booklet for each one of the ten CASES included. Add pen and paper and you're ready. 

You're gonna investigate clues trying to figure out what happened in S.H.'s style. 
Choose who to speak to and where to go with a high degree of freedom ("uhmm, maybe we should talk with Mr.Ragland's tailor"). Very challenging, well written and rewarding when you are able to connect the dots, and even when you are not. 

If you like the theme and the play style it's an absolute MUST. THE best game for couples. A lot of text, buy it in you own language.
Yes it has a life span, but THIS IS NOT an issue. You will get 10 nights you will remember for the rest of your life xD

RATING: 8

Possibly the best 'paragraph' game? You will have to make an educated guess to get to the final answer as it isn't handed to you on a plate. The game heavily rewards attention to detail.

RATING: 9
Extremely well themed mystery game (despite a slight American smack to the dialogue), with intuitive game play and a skeletal framework of simple rules where the players really can explore and sleuth as they wish within the confines of the games casebook. The casebooks which are stand alone or playable as a series of crimes to solve are progressively more and more tricky and devious. It is NOT easy to win a case even if you draw mostly the right conclusions. Though the built in lack of replay-ability is an obvious flaw its not as bad as it seems. So tricky and detailed are many of the cases after a few years its nigh on impossible to remember them and they can be re-attempted without them being too spoiled.  A very good co-op game even for nongamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
By now it is certainly cliché to say that you experience this game, more than you play it, but there it is. 

What I love:
-co-op OR competitive!
-thematic - even though the contents of this box are spartan, you do begin to feel like you're in London in the late 19th century.
-challenging - you're going to burn some gray matter with these cases.
-genuinely engaging / immersive - when you're in the middle of a case, it consumes you!
-pride - when you're reading the various statements of the people you meet with as you try to solve the case, opportunity is there to cheat, and to read other little bits, only, that would rob you of your accomplishment!

What I find annoying:
-Obviously there are typos, everyone knows this.
-This was an expensive game ($70 here in Australia), and while the experience has definitely been worth it (so far), it seems hard to justify the cost of a 36 year old game comprised entirely of printed materials of average quality. For that price, I should like to see nicer paper, more artwork, finer construction, larger fonts (more on that next), a bigger map, and is it too much to ask that you include a notebook, since it's absolutely indispensable to game play??? Jesus.
-the font size, and design is just asinine. Reading the directory requires an electron microscope for instance, and that is no exaggeration. Okay, maybe a little. They've had almost 4 (FOUR!) decades to remedy these issues... Lift ya game, mates!
-Sherlock Holmes is a dick. I have never liked how absurd and contrived his powers of deduction are meant to be, give me a break! 

This game's pretty great.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is the first modern tabletop game I bought and after buying and playing ~70 other games, this still stays at the top of my list of Best Games.

I love everything about it:
• map!
• story
• having to think like a detective
• interaction with other players, testing theories with each other, seeing how other people’s different strengths come out in how they solve problems
• simple set up and easy to get started
• leaves you thinking about the cases long after: What could we have done differently?

Minor quibbles include:
• double translation errors in Ystari edition and some mucking about with original cases that don’t necessarily make them more coherent — I’ll blame the translation, which ought to be fixed in the Space Cowboys edition
• Wiggins (who we are supposed to be in the story) doesn’t always ask about things we want to ask about, like clues in the room we’re in, for example

Beating Sherlock is not easy, nor should it be. For me, this game requires a satisfying amount of deduction, induction, and abduction.

This game will not be as enjoyable for:
• people who are unaccustomed to thinking logically and highly rationally
• people who insist on realism
• people who become too fixated with a theory and can’t amend when presented with contradictory information
• people who aren’t in the mood to take in a great deal of information and sift through it all for key clues
• people who don’t enjoy puzzles

RATING: 8
2013 Secret Santa.

Outstanding, very impressive. Minimal rules overhead, well written (the occasional typo excepted) and a wealth of period detail provided. The newspapers in particular are superb; they have obviously been researched very well.

As for gameplay, our first case (The Munitions Magnate) was satisfyingly complex, with plenty of red herrings and blind alleys. The game works very well with two players and with an eye to exploring the case and generating a credible, convincing theory as opposed to racing to out-perform Holmes.

A word on the Ystari case rewrites: we've played a couple of these and in each instance have 'solved' the cases in accordance with the Ystari rewrites. So, thumbs up to Ystari.

RATING: 6.125
I love, love, love:
- solving mysteries!
- getting to study a map and newspaper and interview people around London like Holmes

I dislike:
- ALL. THE. TYPOS. WOW.
- that some of Sherlock's conclusions make no sense in how they're reached
- that the game kind of encourages you to go to extra places that have nothing to do with the mystery so you can answer the questions for points, but the more you move around, the less points you get...

Final verdict: Enjoyable game, but it has no replayability, really, unless you can totally forget the stories and go back maybe after a couple of years to replay them. Glad it was a gift, as this game could easily have been just as good as a free print-and-play.

RATING: 10
One of the best games I've ever played.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Even though I only got above 0 pts once, these were somewhat enjoyable to go through.  I liked a little bit of puzzle solving, and seeing Holmes leaps of logic were fun, although sometimes annoying in that Homles always knows when people will be at home instead of at work.  

If you like hard deduction games, and don't treat it like you have to beat Holmes, you'll probably like this.  Treat Case 1 as a tutorial on how to actually play the game.  Your first lead should just about always be to visit the scene of the crime.  I would advise playing this not as a solo like i did, but with 2 so that you can bounce ideas off each other.

If I couldn't make more progress I just skipped to the questions and didn't care about my score.

A couple of things I didn't care for: 
- red herrings or dead ends were fleshed out quite a bit so either you are on the right track, or you are on the wrong track and won't know it until you visit another 4 or 5 leads.
- you'll rarely, if ever, find actual proof for any of the people that did it.  You'll have to make some assumptions that seem to fit the evidence and, boom, that's the answer.  Now, after the fact, Scotland Yard would have to go and visit all of the leads I actually visited to actually build a case to prosecute.
- The standard people that help are a real hit or miss, even when you think they should have something.


Case 1: -5 pts.  I visited 12 more spots than Holmes.  I didn't get why he would visit one of the spots, which, when reviewing after the fact, didn't really give me much more info than I already had.  Other than that, I got the case wrong, but it was a good learning game to understand how tight Holmes works.

Case 2: -10 pts.  I went down the red herring trails of missing jewel and the nephew of one of the Tontine people.  I didn't even think of heading to the theatre.  This case was a little better than the first one with regards to actually working through things in a more step by step manner.

Case 3: skipped as I heard there were some changes that didn't make sense and they changed the killer but didn't update everything so you could reach a different conclusion.

Case 4: -45 pts.  I didn't review the old papers enough to know that the guys were brothers.  Holmes mentions some things that were lost in translation about a park, and he gets info from a telegram that we got by using a lead.

Case 5: -10 pts.  I didn't get the boarding house from backtracking, but the hotel, so I missed out on half the plot.  The date being so important didn't make sense that 5 was the key when the month was different as well, so it could have been 2, because 2 months off.

Case 6: -25 pts.  I guessed at the beginning that 2 of the murders were done by the last guy but then changed it as went along.  I don't like that you waste leads if you don't do things in the right order.  Why would I assume that the captain/first mate are at their homes and not at work at the Shipping company (3 leads).  Without going somewhere else you don't realize that you can just go to the First mate.  Also, there is no reason to assume that the last killer could not have done the first 2 killings.

Case 7: -60 pts.  This was an interesting case but man, was it tough to put the clues together. You are supposed to assume that the a guy whose partner died had a cell mate with the same name as someone that left a personal ad with just first names and then connect his girlfriend to it by finding another story that has the same first name.  Obviously, those two women have to be the same :)

Case 8: 15 pts.  The most interesting case so far, and the one where i actually solved just about all of it.  I didn't gather that the securities were being stolen along the way, and wound up using 14 more leads to get a more solid case.  Holmes conclusions, while I agree with them seemed a bit circumstantial whereas my leads gave me more hard proof.  There was a timing issue with Moran in that it said he was in 2 places around the same time.  I think it was a misprint as it wasn't brought up again.

Case 9: 0 pts.  
Nitpicks about this case:
- Holmes decides he wants to visit 2 out of the 3 staff, which are the only ones that provide info.  How does he know that the 3rd won't know anything?  
- Without visiting 1 person at the beginning I missed out on names that would have clued me in on what the list of sales were.  
- They made a big point of saying there was nothing in the guys stomach but yet a bite was missing from the biscuit.  I thought this meant he hadn't taken a bit at all which through me off.
- Holmes mentions that Jasper should know more about something at the beginning and then he doesn't even use him.

Case 10: -25 pts
I guessed early that there was a Thomas Crowne Affair thing going on and Norris let someone in.  I picked up that Cole was involved, although Holmes conclusions aren't supported by any facts other than Norris/Cole had met (which Holmes doesn't know since he didn't go to the bar).  He assumes it's all fakes because there was some non-old paint which didn't discount that the other paintings could have been real.  This case, while interesting, seemed to have a lot more assumptions on Holmes part.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
While the translation occasionally makes one grind their teeth, the core game here is brilliant fun if your audience is used to classic adventure games on the PC.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Even though some of the cases are a little frustrating, this game offers an experience like no other.  This game feels almost like Myst, you're left to your own deductive devices to solve the crime, the game itself will offer you no assistance whatsoever.  

At the beginning of a case, you're given some details of a crime, and then you're thrown out on the streets and told to go explore London and solve it.  The game only moves forward when you actively make a decision to go somewhere and talk to someone.  You can take as long as you want to ponder what you've learned and hypothesize.  The case only ends when you think you have enough information to deduce what happened.  

While solving a case and getting a high score feels great, even getting a case completely wrong and earning an abysmally low score can still be fun.  Once, we got so lost during a case that it became a disastrously bad experience we couldn't wait to be over, but then we wanted to go right into the next case and keep going.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I went into the first scenario thinking we'd need to build a waterproof case, especially after Holmes' admonishment to stick to the facts in the introduction. Of course, that meant we visited far too many places and talked to too many people and still didn't have a smoking gun at the end. Because the game doesn't have any. It's not so much about collecting solid evidence as it is about building a house of cards with just a few tidbits of information.

Obviously, we adapted accordingly on later cases. Some of them require huge leaps of faith, some solutions seem a little far-fetched, and at least for the first few cases we never got anywhere near Holmes' scores but the game was always greatly entertaining regardless. And that's kind of the point.

The only downside is the limited replayability. It's pretty much one and done.

RATING: 7
Of course, this is not so much a "board game" as an interactive story.  There is a scoring system, but it's a terrible idea to follow it too much to the letter as it encourages you solve the case quickly and try to do as well as Sherlock Homes (who always scores 100 points).  This means that you miss a lot of the flavour (and this whole game is flavour) if you try to solve the case too quickly without visiting interesting (if not possibly vital) areas.  As long as you play in role and don't try to "game" the game by visiting every single bloody location, then you should be fine.  It was a fun experience!  Some of the narrative is a bit heavy-handed, but enough fake-twiddling of one's fake-moustache and bad accents can get you through even the most over-wrought phrases.

RATING: 7.5
I know that one day I'll solve all the cases and the game will become a cardboard paperweight.
But for now it is a unique and challenging play experience. There really is nothing like it, and every case has thrown at least one of the people playing it off on a hunt for red herrings.
Try it out if you can find a cheap sale on Ebay or a trade. Then give it to your friends so the fun can live on in another generation.

UPDATE - I took a break for over a year, and went back to some of the cases.  I sort of remember many details, but it's still fun to figure out again.  And I can act as the reader for another player while they figure it out, which is more of a blast than it sounds like it should be.

RATING: 7
Bought September 2014. Rating based on two plays.

Played through case 1 of [thing=2511][/thing] with six friends sitting around an open fire, which I think is probably the perfect atmosphere, and was thoroughly satisfying. Solved the case (cooperatively) and scored 75 points versus Sherlock's 100 (or 85 with less strict scoring).

Case 2: oh dear, -5 points (15 with less strict scoring) versus Sherlock's 100. This one was a bit more opaque. We had the right general idea, but couldn't work out where to go to get more detailed information.

It's more of a sandboxy Choose Your Own Adventure story than a game. The cleverly layered narrative gives it an edge for me over other storytelling games I've tried (I'm looking at you, [thing=34119][/thing]).

RATING: 10
I'm the biggest Sherlock Holmes fan I've ever met.  It took all of my effort to not buy this for myself as it was an ideal Christmas gift and no one ever knows what to give me.  My brother and I have been combining wits and are working through the cases together.  The scoring system is busted in that you're scored for your ability to answer questions in Part Two, but Holmes doesn't bother with those.  You lose points for taking extra turns, but you can't answer Part Two questions without taking extra turns.  Without paying attention to the scores, the game is perfect.  I love it.  It's amazing.  The more thought you put into the case the more enjoyable it is.

UPDATE:  Case #3 is total bullsh!t. There isn't enough evidence for a reliable deduction.

SUMMARY: It has a few flaws, but overall it's a winner.  Just loses some points for not being replayable.

UPDATE: I believe this to be the most thematic game in the entire BGG database.  It's the most exciting and memorable gaming experience I've had in a long time.  Fantastic game!

RATING: 9.5
Get over it. 
You're not as smart as you think you are. 
I know you. You're the one who watches CSI shows while shouting advice at the screen. You think your Rick freakin' Castle, or Dr.Gregory "get bent" House. 
You think you know everything.
Well, you don't. 
Because Sherlock Holmes knows everything, and if you want to take a lesson in humility, just sit down next to him and talk your way through the solution you came up with for one of the mysteries in this game.
ME: "So, I began to think the deceased was wrought with overwhelming guilt, and in a final act of contrition, killed himself with one of his military collectibles."
SHERLOCK: "That's remarkable.  Remarkably wrong! Aside from being a mouth-breathing moron, you've also managed to twist the evidence in this case into a tale of sheer fantasy. Shall I have a carriage come round for you? I honestly wonder how you find your way home at night."

Yeah, it's like that.

This is the BEST story-telling game you will play. All others will fall short and leave you wondering why you bothered picking them up in the first place.
You can teach someone to play this game in 2 minutes. "Read the initial mystery, now follow a lead either by looking at the map of London, or checking the included directory of persons and places and obtain a code. Look that code up and read the next clue. Then keep going till you think you've solved the mystery."
That's it. 
As simple as it is, you feel like a REAL detective. You don't play this game so much as you run an actual investigation. You decide with whom you will speak, when to visit the crime scene (if at all), and when to involve other professionals like the medical examiner, or Scotland Yard. It's all up to you, but things are left wonderfully vague enough for you to make leaps in logic that actually pay off, or send you down the wrong trail.
That's another brilliant part of this game: wrong trails are equally supported with information. So if you think the murder suspect killed himself, you'll find information to support that- even though it's wrong, but it's your fault for not paying attention to the real clues. 
There is an included lecture in the instruction booklet from Sherlock Holmes who warns you to not let theories twist facts, and he's right. If nothing else, this game could be presented as a course in information management, or discernment in logical thinking.

As you follow each lead, you realize that getting to the truth isn't easy, especially if you want to beat Holmes at solving the case, which you can do.
Maybe.
If you're good. I mean VERY good.
If you keep your logic sound, and let the facts speak for themselves, occasionally, you'll get lucky. When you follow the right path of leads, the solution presents itself in a neat little package, but there are other ancillary mysteries going on, and when you get to the questions at the end of the mystery you realized that you missed something. Yes, you did, but now it's too late. And Sherlock is sitting in the parlor, ready to discuss his solution and compare it with yours. And you know he's going to make you feel like a third grader.

I love this game, and can't wait to play it with a group. Oh, didn't I tell you?
You can play this game solo.
That's right, just you and the case book and a few resources. It's the best solo experience I've had in gaming. 
Not into the lone-wolf thing? How about a game to play with your spouse or partner?  Here it is.
Get this game before it's gone, because I don't think it will make another release. 
Yes, this game is actually a re-release of the original game that came out in the 80's. There was also a very badly executed "Full motion Video" version of it for computer systems back in the day. I never played it, but I did see a demo version. It looked bad.

On the negative side: There are glaring TYPOS in the rulebook and throughout the mystery books. It's horrible how this oversight makes the game look like a quickly-printed mess that didn't get even a basic proof read. 
VERY LAZY. Holmes wouldn't have put up with that, and certainly not Watson. Shame on you game publisher. This game deserves nothing but a stellar package, and you blew it.

RATING: 8
Fantastic. Players are given the starting scenario for a mystery and then allowed to explore freely in any number of directions-- visit the crime scene, interview a suspect, check the paper for relevant stories. After you believe you've solved the crime, you answer questions and are scored on not only your accuracy, but the number of clues it required.

The writing is excellent and perfectly matches the style of the original Holmes stories. The game play is reminiscent of the old "Choose Your Own Adventure" books, but with much more free-form choices.

RATING: 6
This is my rating after the first three cases based upon averaging out the score for each:

- First case: 9. Really fun, well written, interesting clues to follow that definitely all have their own twists and turns but with the true crime becoming evident very organically and in a way that gives you that "a ha!" feeling.

- Second case: 7. Fun, but with some rather confusing/misleading clues that I wonder were written poorly due to translation issues. Still an interesting plot to uncover that definitely made sense as more evidence was uncovered, albeit in not quite as interesting a way as the first case. 

- Third case: 1. Awful. Horribly misleading clues, nonsensical plot, not fun to play at all. At various times felt like every single lead was being followed, and nothing was becoming more clear. Had the "true" plot figured out early based on a hunch, but after following leads to confirm, it didn't seem like anything but the hunch corroborated the theory, only to find out it indeed was the correct conclusion. I would practically say this case was broken, except for that it CAN be figured out...so long as you ignore a lot of evidence to the contrary for no good reason, and only focus on the snippets that the writers apparently wanted you to focus on? One of the more frustrating experiences I can think of. And due to the nature of some of the clues and case conclusions in previous cases, there was no way of knowing if something was being missed, or if something just wasn't there. 

I have since read that case 3 is infamous in this collection, but am pretty disappointed to learn that the most recent version (which is what I have) was supposed to "fix" problems like those that were encountered. It's disappointing to think that at least 1/10th of the game is just a complete waste of time.

Hopefully the rest of the cases trend more towards the first two, but even so, it's still disappointing to have wasted so much time and effort on something that was designer error/publishing negligence.

RATING: 9
At the time of this writing, I have only played the first case for this game, but wow!  A deduction game where you are in the world of Sherlock Holmes.  Technically I think you play the part of one of Holmes men and not Holmes himself.

The open-endedness of the game is its strength.  You are given a paragraph of what happens at a site and that is it.  Based upon what you read and what you currently know you need to decide which location to visit.  You can become easily stuck if you do not see a location in your directories or do not think a location is mentioned and thus do not look for it.

Notes are mandatory for the game as are the occasional leaps of logical faith.

-----
Editted: Having now played half a dozen times, I have increased my ranking to a 9.  This is a perfect game for a group of friends to gather to solve the crime.  I found it is best not to worry about the scoring in it and enjoy the adventure in front of you...and to realize how very much you are unlike the famous detective.

RATING: 7.5
Definitely a sometimes game, something I really have to be in the mood for to play. Though when I'm in the mood for it it's pretty great. Definitely a bit wonky though; anyplace you go to follow a lead has a static set of information you learn. As a result if you go to a particular place with the intention of learning one thing it might just not get brought up if it's not something the game considered and instead you learn some other stuff that maybe you weren't on the trail of. If and when this happens it really takes you out of the game. I think in general there are a few things like this that are inherent limitations of trying to do something like this with a static finite amount of information available, but overall it's an ambitious idea and it mostly works.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
With the right group, this is a blast!  It's basically a choose-your-adventure coop game where the group is presented with a mystery and then you get to try to solve it.  You've got a map of London with many many places numbered (and a directory of who lives where) plus a list of special informants.  You decide what location to go to and then look it up in the mystery book and read what happens.  There is no chance element.  You are trying to figure it out in the least number of visits.  When you think you have it, you go to the Master Detective and he asks a series of questions.  If you can answer them, you win!  If he asks you questions about people you've never heard about, then you get a sinking feeling.  :)  If you get stuck you can also visit him for clues.  The mysteries are a good level of difficulty and with interesting twists.  Very atmospheric and fun!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Pretty fun, and a completely unique experience. The font and translation are bad-but-functional and there are a lot of typos. Some of the solutions are kind of dumb (I'm looking at you case #3). Make sure you get the errata. 

I suggest playing against each other rather than cooperatively, as cooperatively can be frustrating when you don't agree on how to proceed. This could have been a 9 or better with better writing and a few tweaks.

Edit: after playing more, this game is ruined for us by the pervasive errors and bad design of the cases. We're no longer willing to sit and agonize over a case for hours, not knowing whether we're just missing something, or if the solution is something stupid that no human would think of, or if some vital typo/error is throwing us off. Ugh, this game should be a 10. Instead it is a 4.

RATING: 5
2013-05-14

Initial Rating: 6.0 (May 2013)

Good game experience. This is not a game for everybody but it certainly appeals to me. The game can be short or long depending on how well do you play it, the game components are great! The old newspapers are great to read :D, the atmosphere is very well done. Very novel mechanics (or at leasrt very different from what I’m accustomed to).

On the bad side, the language barrier is great for some players (if only one or two players know English they have to carefully read and convey the clues to the others), also I think the game is best played as a 2 or 3 player game, with more I feel the game begins to bog down as everyone discuss. I don’t like that we are supposed to solve the mystery with only 4 or 5 clues (as Sherlock would have done it),  I feel most of the game is wasted if we play this way, I would like to explore the world at heart because it is very detailed (I shudder at the effort required to do this and it is a shame to waste it), that is, I don’t want to optimize the result for this game (winning it in 3 steps), I want the experience. As the game only comes with 10 cases I don’t think I will buy it, the game replayability is practically zero. 

For now I’m rating it a 6.0 because I feel the game has potential, but I didn’t fully enjoy my only play. 

I remember I had a PC game with this title, perhaps the cases are the same? I was too young to play it correctly and I don’t remember, however I want to buy it for the iPad so I can play it solo (and I don’t want to play solo games ever, still Sherlock Holmes calls to me).

Bottom line, I want to play this game again (I even requested a second play after the first one but I was shot down), I think the rating will go up with more plays, but only If I’m allowed to really explore the game. This is the only game I had have urges to play solo.

RATING: 8
Collect clues through reading and solve crimes in as few turns as possible. You can work together to solve or compete to solve it more quickly than the others. Each turn you can look up a person or location mentioned in an earlier clue and hope to get something useful. The game is about deduction, so you will find scant hard evidence here. 

Very well-written. Amazingly thought out and put together. A game unlike any other. Replayability is low and occassionally passages will assume you've learned something you haven't, but these are minor quibbles. If it sounds like a fun idea to you, then you won't be disappointed.

RATING: 7
Very unique, clever idea, and the recent reprint is of high quality. It's an excellent family or party game (assuming everyone is an adult though; likely too taxing for kids), and many people who loathe to play board games love to give this one a go.

I would rate it higher, but unfortunately there are a lot of typos in the new reprint, and some of the cases are "broken" in that they require ridiculous leaps of deduction. If five bright adults (including a medical doctor, a pharmaceutical chemist, a classical composer, and a programming language developer) spend nearly 6 hours on a single case and only get one minor question right at the end, I think something is a bit off.

But still, it's the journey that matters the most. Even though the endings are rather anticlimactic and sometimes blatantly unfair, the process is still great fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a difficult game to rank, because there really isn't a lot of game in it. There is a great experience in playing the game, but scoring is really not necessary and collecting the information necessary to score just gets in the way of the experience. After a few plays, I have decided to not worry about scoring and just follow the leads in the case and enjoy the story that unfolds.
It is also difficult to rank this game due to the absolutely miserable production quality of this game. The concept is great, the potential endless, but the game falls short. As it is, I have ranked this game too high for its quality because it is rare in concept and I want it to be so good.
The material quality is OK, but the graphic design is horrible and the editing of all textual materials is even worse. This would be bad enough in a game that is only dependent on these materials for conveying the rules, but in this case, the text is the game. Fortunately, several BGG users have uploaded fixes to some of the errors in the cases (which, in the instance of Case 3 would otherwise make the case completely unsolvable). However, beyond the material errors in the text, there are so many typos and the text so unreadable (light script on a mottled, brown background) that the narrative is destroyed. The map of London is similarly difficult to read, so any time that a case requires searching for street names, we often end up skipping that part of the investigation. 
It is a shame that the publisher, knowing that this was a highly anticipated reprint, spent so little effort in its production. Honestly, shame on Ystari. I am not one to accuse a publisher of a "money grab," but seriously, this game has the worst quality control of any game that I own. It was obviously just thrown into the market because there was a demand for it.

We both enjoyed the game and found working together to be a lot of fun. However, I wouldn't want to play this with more than two.

The game content is extremely well conceived. The work that went into making each mystery is staggering. Clues and story weaved together and carefully portioned out along with red herrings and secondary lines of investigation. When you take a step back after the mystery is solved it's hard not to be impressed with the quality of it all. 

My one nit-pick at this point is the font used. The hand writing script is hard to read and likely the cause of several typos found in the text. It does make it harder to accidentally read clues you aren't entitled to, but I would have preferred a more mundane typeface.

RATING: 5
Of the things you might expect from a paragraph-based Sherlock Holmes game, Consulting Detective does at least one thing pretty well: the writing and characterization is colourful, varied, occasionally amusing, and just about the right length. When it comes to deduction, however, the logical path you're expected to take through these cases is anything but rigorous. If not sooner, this will become obvious when you're reading Holmes's exposés, which largely account for the facts of each case, and don't overtly contradict them, yet don't actually prove much, depend on assumptions, extrapolations and conjecture, and blatantly rely on information not covered in the selection of paragraphs Holmes is said to have used. Consequently, the initially appealing prospect of solving a case "just like Holmes" is a red herring, and truly shooting for such a feat means depriving yourself of reading and puzzling over the majority of clues before arbitrarily deciding on a hypothesis - which is likely to be incomplete anyway, given that you don't know beforehand exactly what you're expected to account for, adding to the impossibility of a solution that is both rapid and conclusive. So what we have here is a nice piece of creative writing, even a decent brain teaser, but don't expect a well-defined board game where the proper use of logic is rewarded, and don't be surprised if the end of each case leaves you feeling you want to punch Holmes in the gut.

Thrifted on 7/12 2017.

RATING: N/A
An old classic with a new face.  This printing is tops.  A cooperative (or solo) game where you try to beat Sherlock Holmes at solving several cases by using clues from the casebook, newspapers, a register of London's people and businesses, and a map.  One to make you scratch your head and try to figure out the cases.  I love this style and wish more games were like it.  The weakness is obviously that once you play through the cases, you know the outcome, so it is pretty much a play it once and toss it type of game.  There is no replayability.  That doesn't stop me from loving it, though.  I just want more like this.  :-)
